    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

  <span id="freeText14034250859344551777" style="display:none">On a lazy Sunday morning, two young people are wheeled into Room No. 509 of GKL super specialty hospital.<br /><br />A brilliant nineteen year old medical student, suffering from an incurable, fatal disease hurtling her at a slow, painful, uncertain death.<br /><br />A wasteful twenty five year old drug addict, with no appreciation of life, with every organ system of his body slowly shutting down.<br /><br />Two prodigious doctors, fighting their own demons from the past, try to keep these two patients alive, putting their medical licenses at risk.<br /><br />Death looms in the tiny 12X13 foot room as they fight for every breath of their lives, even as the doctors put them through unapproved experimental treatments to prolong their lives.<br /><br />How will the last month of pain and struggle change their lives? How will it transform the doctors who work steadfastly to make them live a little longer?</span>

<div id="review_589116798" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/589116798" />
    <a title="Surbhi Arora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18740440-surbhi-arora"><img alt="Surbhi Arora" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/589116798?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Surbhi Arora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Surbhi Arora" href="/user/show/18740440-surbhi-arora">Surbhi Arora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer589116798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2947881380919117633">Tears-in-my-eyes!<br/><br/>It is terrific how life can teach us its most important lessons in the sweetest way. Through a novel- non living thing no less! How were I to know that this novel is gonna reiterate one of life's incredibly important lesson.<br/><br/>"YOLO". You Only Live Once. Albeit, Dushyant got to live twice.<br/><br/>The story as such has been amazingly spun. This web has all that it needs to entertain, teach, and make you cry. The characters are woven in a way that you can instantly connect with them. If not </span>
  <span id="freeText2947881380919117633" style="display:none">Tears-in-my-eyes!<br /><br />It is terrific how life can teach us its most important lessons in the sweetest way. Through a novel- non living thing no less! How were I to know that this novel is gonna reiterate one of life's incredibly important lesson.<br /><br />"YOLO". You Only Live Once. Albeit, Dushyant got to live twice.<br /><br />The story as such has been amazingly spun. This web has all that it needs to entertain, teach, and make you cry. The characters are woven in a way that you can instantly connect with them. If not with their profession or past, then by their "place in this world", their "identity".<br /><br />Frankly, I liked it better than If Its Not Forever! I think perhaps Durjoy Dutta attemted a Nicholas Sparks here! I say this because it is high on first crushes and love and also,the girl dies. Sorry to break it to those who still hadnt read the novel. You know you should! And it wont cost you a fortune. (Y)<br /><br />My favorite:<br />Arman took out what he had been carrying with him for weeks now. He dangled it in front of her. It was gold chain, the yellowness of gold had somewhat waned away,and hanging beneath it was a small diamond of 3 carats, and it was beyond beautiful.<br /><br />'This is for you,' he said and gingerly took Pihu's hand into his and wrapped it thrice around her limp, senseless wrist. Pihu's eyes sparkled as she gazed at her newly acquired possession.<br /><br />'That is beautiful.'<br /><br />'It pales in comparison to you. You're the most beautiful thing I have ever considered my own. Before you came along, I was a loner,someone who didn't care about anything but himself, his work, his obsession. But one fine day, you walked into my life, with the help of crutches, no less,and turned it upside down. For the first time, I loved someone more than I have loved myself,' he said.<br /><br />'You make even dying beautiful,' she purred.<br /><br /><br />In crux, you cannot- just cannot- miss this novel. I always considered Durjoy Dutta to be trash, but now, I can only applaud and perhaps salute. This novel is "Life" personified. "I cry," Till My Last Breath!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2947881380919117633" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Anindita Roy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12369217-anindita-roy"><img alt="Anindita Roy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400558278p2/12369217.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/510742304?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anindita Roy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anindita Roy" href="/user/show/12369217-anindita-roy">Anindita Roy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer510742304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6478801069547621991">This was the first book I read of this author. Seeing the titles of his other books, I was reluctant to buy n read it as I am wary of Indian college romantic tales. However, I had no option left as I badly needed a book to read during my train journey. And this was one of the few decent books in English in the single bookstore at one of the railway stations my train had stopped at and the only which I had not read yet. So, I bought it..I usually can't sleep in train journeys, so started reading </span>
  <span id="freeText6478801069547621991" style="display:none">This was the first book I read of this author. Seeing the titles of his other books, I was reluctant to buy n read it as I am wary of Indian college romantic tales. However, I had no option left as I badly needed a book to read during my train journey. And this was one of the few decent books in English in the single bookstore at one of the railway stations my train had stopped at and the only which I had not read yet. So, I bought it..I usually can't sleep in train journeys, so started reading this book after everyone in my friends group went to sleep. <br />Contrary to what I had expected, this book wasn't a weary or bubbly love story, but the story of two lives-one weary and the other bubbly...How the two lives meet in a Hospital room and become..No, not lovers (sorry for the spoiler)..but great friends and true room-mates, while finding true loves and rethinking their lives..The characters reminded me of some very important persons in my life..Pihu reminded me my younger sister who is no more now...Thus, this story touched me in different ways.<br /><br />For the author, I would say that I really liked his way of describing life accounts in a lucid manner without using the cliches and bromides that young Indian authors fill their books with..and yet retaining the freshness of youth, with its mix of innocence, mistakes, regrets and pain...Yes, I really liked the book and giving it four stars!!!:):) Cheers!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6478801069547621991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6804800020068536715">A very mature work by Durjoy. He has come of age and this one is a heart melting one.<br/>The story is about 2 terminally ill patients Dushyant and Peehu and their doctors Arman and Zarah. How they get attached for life at the hospital is the plot.<br/>The story is touching and makes us realise the importance of each moment in our life. <br/>A must read especially for those who have hefty complaints in life for the silliest of reasons.</span>

  <span id="freeText10977936342250825179" style="display:none">Ok...first things first - I had vowed to stay away from his books after I finished "Someone Like you". But since I had no other book to read I started with this one reluctantly. And am glad I did! This is by far Durjoy's BEST book.I think his solo writings are much better than collaborations, having read ALL of his books.I found in two places where the names of the characters are muddled...it still is a fabulous read.Its engrosses you with a heart wrenching story of love,life,loss,hope and friendship.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer560972296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15915364598839287331">Well, as a beginning, this review is biased...just a few factors which make it biased:-<br/><br/>a. I am a girl..<br/>b. I am a girl who loves being a girl..<br/>c. I am a girl who is easy on tears...doesn't really takes much to make her eyes wet...not a major melodrama<br/>d. I am a seriously hopelessly romantic girl who knows dreamworld is restricted to dreamworld and still believes that one does get the dream come true in real...<br/><br/>And still, I won't give it a 5 star...it's a highly unrealistic book (thankfully, it stil</span>
  <span id="freeText15915364598839287331" style="display:none">Well, as a beginning, this review is biased...just a few factors which make it biased:-<br /><br />a. I am a girl..<br />b. I am a girl who loves being a girl..<br />c. I am a girl who is easy on tears...doesn't really takes much to make her eyes wet...not a major melodrama<br />d. I am a seriously hopelessly romantic girl who knows dreamworld is restricted to dreamworld and still believes that one does get the dream come true in real...<br /><br />And still, I won't give it a 5 star...it's a highly unrealistic book (thankfully, it still chose the more probably person to live)...the paper quality is bed (yeah, only I can comment on paper quality when my eyes are still moist with the expected but still heart-breaking ending)...the editing is worse (how can you, seriously how can you...from the writer to the first proof reader, to the friends you share the manuscripts and last but not the least, editor, not realize that they are goofing up the names...calling X in between Y's narrative and remembering Z out of blue)...a mistake beyond forgiveness...<br /><br />But still, the novel does what it can...what it was planned to do...give you a character-sketch of few really twisted people...some by choice, some by fate...solve things out for few...tries to be realistic by putting few out of scene...a perfect love (though I want to read real more about Dr. Arman....are you going to write more Durjoy...or can I copy lift the character and at least write a short story for myself as far as he is concerned...but then don't write a thing, if you want to take it the Ravinder Singh way of 'Can love happen twice')<br /><br />All in all, a quick read, which would keep you glued...not make you crib too about the erratic story lines we Indian authors follow...and of course is any day way better than the usual college love stories (even if this one is unbelievable love story, it's better than that!!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15915364598839287331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4524474584356690405">INSPIRING LOVE STORY ...................<br/><br/>Waoo , An amazing read from Durjoy Datta , which takes the readers on the journey to so many emotions . I finished the book and tears enveloped my eyes . Its rare . But it happened ..... This book left a deep impression on me , a feeling to be proud of every one I've in my life . For everything I've . Human Character it is , that we always ignore that we have , but realised after losing them . <br/><br/>A Truly compelling read which let the reader hook to the book t</span>
  <span id="freeText4524474584356690405" style="display:none">INSPIRING LOVE STORY ...................<br /><br />Waoo , An amazing read from Durjoy Datta , which takes the readers on the journey to so many emotions . I finished the book and tears enveloped my eyes . Its rare . But it happened ..... This book left a deep impression on me , a feeling to be proud of every one I've in my life . For everything I've . Human Character it is , that we always ignore that we have , but realised after losing them . <br /><br />A Truly compelling read which let the reader hook to the book till its very end . Book Revolves around Two Patients , Pihu and Dushyant &amp; Two Doctors Arman &amp; Zarah , treating them . Pihu , on one side is a brilliant medical student who self-diagnosed ALS ,one which was diagnosed for Stephen Hawking .She counts every extra breath as blessing. After meeting number of Doctors , she ended up getting admitted at GKL Hospital under Dr. Arman's eye . Arman is portrayed as a genius , one who knew he was gifted . He could see beyond the obvious &amp; take radical decisions that no else would dare to take , as he did in Pihu's case .<br />On other Hand , Dushyant is a self spoiled , intelligent brat who was brought to hospital after passing out in a drinking session a night ago . He drink himself to death after his girlfriend left him .Later coming to hospital , he found himself being fitted with Dr. Zarah . Dr. Zarah , had joined the hospital as intrern under Arman , and was struggling from her dark past , a cripple relationship with her parents especially her Dad . Dushyant too was given up by his parents . Their Love story realise that sometimes if we are broken then someone damaged suits us well . <br />Till the Last Breath....is a deeply sensitive story that reminds us what it means to alive and I think this is the only book so far , whose every single protagonist dictates an awe-inspiring story .<br /><br />MUST READ !!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4524474584356690405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText17685210462994956818" style="display:none">I am not a big fan of Durjoy Datta. I have read a few of his books - You were my crush, oh yes I am single. They were a disaster. Then came his book, If its not forever. I didnt want to read it. But the title of the book made me read it. I wasnt disappointed. It had love stories with travelling. A perfect blend. And plot seemed convincing. It gave the impression of drama. And, I hate dramas or literature.<br /><br />Within a week after the book was out, it was in my hands. I just completed reading Jeffery Archer's Twist in the Tale. After reading a few short stories with twisting ends at its best, I was ready to take on a boring read. That is what I had in my about this book.<br /><br />The book in my hand seemed alien to me. I didn't see many books with white covers. The front cover blended with the papers inside. Also, the book was very light for a 240 pages book. A riffle through the pages told that the paper was very light weighted - indicated low or high quality, I don't know.<br /><br />I started reading it.<br /><br />There are in total five main characters of this book - Arman Kashyup, Kajal Khurana, Pihu Malhotra, Dishyant Roy, Zarah Mirza. Arman is a doctor; Dushyant is a patient, who is at the brink of his mortality, admitted in Arman's hospital. Pihu is young, normal medicine student. But fate doesn't play fair with her. <div id="review_713201551" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/713201551" />
    <a title="Shivani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13633916-shivani"><img alt="Shivani" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/713201551?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shivani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shivani" href="/user/show/13633916-shivani">Shivani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer713201551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15957577850821780259">I liked the concept of the book- An overachiever diagnosed with ALS. A drunkard devoid of love. In fact, the story was very realistically set. The author described well the struggles of the protagonists to come to terms with their fates. I even loved the character Dushyant, despite what is made of him. But somehow, I felt like it was dragged. The 10 chapters in between seemed like a struggle to me. And the editing, oh the editing was horrible. Grammatical mistakes are still bearable, but 'spelli</span>
  <span id="freeText15957577850821780259" style="display:none">I liked the concept of the book- An overachiever diagnosed with ALS. A drunkard devoid of love. In fact, the story was very realistically set. The author described well the struggles of the protagonists to come to terms with their fates. I even loved the character Dushyant, despite what is made of him. But somehow, I felt like it was dragged. The 10 chapters in between seemed like a struggle to me. And the editing, oh the editing was horrible. Grammatical mistakes are still bearable, but 'spelling' mistakes? Jeez, that's unforgivable.<br />Anyhow, Pihu's character makes me want to puke in some parts and hug in some. I didn't enjoy hers and Dr. Arman's romance much. I'd liked Zarah's and Dushyant's a lot though. Venky was an odd yet fun addition.<br />In a nutshell, it was a 50-50 bet for me. I liked Dushyant more than Pihu, contrary to what was supposed to be. There were constant ups and downs; The story was not so consistent. However, the ending was very touching. I felt the world stop for a second after I read the last line. <br /><br />So maybe the story doesn't progress so well, but the ending sure leaves you overwhelmed. <br /><br />PS- I don't recommend this book to all the Grey's Anatomy's fans out there. Want Medical Drama? Watch reruns instead. :P</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1318761258" />
    <a title="Rishabh Bhoj" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41665535-rishabh-bhoj"><img alt="Rishabh Bhoj" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427626039p2/41665535.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1318761258?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rishabh Bhoj" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rishabh Bhoj" href="/user/show/41665535-rishabh-bhoj">Rishabh Bhoj</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1318761258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4325771522611945455">My second review on Durjoy's book. The story is worth reading hence I'm here to make a remark. First of all this is one of the very few books which doesn't involve sex. The story is about two patients in room no.- 509, and two doctors trying their best to save their lives, because both are attached to the patients in a more than professional way. <br/>Will they be able to make it? Will their efforts to save the person they hold dearest to their hearts pay off?<br/>That's what the story is all about. The s</span>
  <span id="freeText4325771522611945455" style="display:none">My second review on Durjoy's book. The story is worth reading hence I'm here to make a remark. First of all this is one of the very few books which doesn't involve sex. The story is about two patients in room no.- 509, and two doctors trying their best to save their lives, because both are attached to the patients in a more than professional way. <br />Will they be able to make it? Will their efforts to save the person they hold dearest to their hearts pay off?<br />That's what the story is all about. The story has some beautiful moments. Pihu is exceptionally cute, so is Zara and Kajal. Dushyant is abrasive, stubborn and learns his lesson the hard way. Arman is stern and strict but changes as the novel progresses and the truth behind is facade is also revealed.<br />This poignant tale of love, endeavors to save your loved ones, takes you on a journey that will touch your heart. By the time the you finish reading the book, you'll realize what it really means to be alive.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4325771522611945455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

My shirt is still drenched in my tears. <br/><br/>Every time when i finish reading a book, I feel so happy and proud </span>
  <span id="freeText14463314418153188003" style="display:none">I have never read such a wonderful book in my life !<br />I literally cried like anything at the end. I re-read the last sentence again and again. It never seemed like a story. I felt it was so personal. I'm writing this teary eyed. No book ever influenced me like this one. This is just a masterpiece by Durjoy. Flawless. Pihu wasn't just a fictional character in the book. I...I'm lost for words. My shirt is still drenched in my tears. <br /><br />Every time when i finish reading a book, I feel so happy and proud of myself. But after reading this one, I Could never put the book back down. I held it tightly and was keeping on reading the final chapter and continued crying. <br />This book will always remain close to my heart. It's not just a book. It's more than that. Miss You Pihu ! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15898483188792463108">That was a devastatingly phenomenal book! So much learn from, so much to be grateful about! It made me feel grateful for still breathing and it reminded me of a phrase "Who will cry when you die..." <br/><br/>The characters are so brilliantly written, I had a difficult time deciding on my favourite. But at the end it was Pihu and Arman! If there's true love, then it definitely belonged to the two of them! <br/><br/>Till the last breath... This book will remind me to celebrate the feeling of being alive...<br/>This book </span>
  <span id="freeText15898483188792463108" style="display:none">That was a devastatingly phenomenal book! So much learn from, so much to be grateful about! It made me feel grateful for still breathing and it reminded me of a phrase "Who will cry when you die..." <br /><br />The characters are so brilliantly written, I had a difficult time deciding on my favourite. But at the end it was Pihu and Arman! If there's true love, then it definitely belonged to the two of them! <br /><br />Till the last breath... This book will remind me to celebrate the feeling of being alive...<br />This book made me raise the levels of hope on Indian writing... :)<br />Lastly, I am glad I was alive to read this book! One of the best reads of the year so far! </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3652688480052557166">The story left me totally speechless and tears were flowing freely when I read the epilogue- Dushyant's confession. Someone like Arman and Zarah can always fall in love, someone like Pihu can always fight it till the last breath (boy I have never seen anyone so full of life, even after knowing her days are numbered!) and someone like Dushyant will always get a second chance. Hats off to Durjoy for capturing the essence of life in a single story. :)</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1424236993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13464351965527833096">This is Durjoy Dutta's one of the most mature work till date. Characters are built well. The story goes in such a flow that you will wonder what will happen next. And While all this happens, you will fall in love with the Cute Pihu. <br/><br/>This book makes you realise the value of life.<br/><br/>At the conclusion of this book, I'm sure everyone who read this book had tears in their eyes. That's how good this book is!!<br/><br/>I recommend it!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7981156167800652448">DEPRESSING!!<br/>As i anticipated it to be, it was very depressing or even more. I felt empathetic at times for Pihu and more for her family. And Armaan sounded like a sweetheart. Dushyanat and Zarah were really something, a different pair.<br/><br/>The end made me cry, made me feel that feeling which Dushyanat and Pihu must have felt.<br/><br/>A good read but too emotional and touching.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oqc2DDDJHyd5aj9pZgRLIzElxph/9MGiCHu+69ACApC3xe7oH986WT3UOcLmog03FtuiilzRMR9wjGl0mqenmQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('43iwrYCfblLL6dHFrVnHw8vh+8WO/CkHyV6nB7A/7J/2GmhJr4lLLI9X124t/4HX7B+f163Z2bqxqXCY+ppJlg==')})
  }
